SEC. 1115. U.S. BORDER PATROL ACTIVITIES. 
18
The Chief of the U.S. Border Patrol shall prioritize 
19
the deployment of U.S. Border Patrol agents to as close 
20
to the physical land border as possible, consistent with 
21
border security enforcement priorities and accessibility to 
22

9

10
(a) IN GENERAL.—The Secretary of State shall im-
11

13

15

17
dren, and other individuals from Central America to 
18
the United States. 
19

20

21

22

23
(3) to improve access to justice; 
24

17

SEC. 1010. H–2B EMPLOYER NOTIFICATION REQUIREMENT. 
22
(a) IN GENERAL.—An employer of one or more H– 
23
2B workers shall, within three business days, make elec-
24
04:01 Mar 04, 2022
H6637
411 
•HR 6637 IH
tronic notification, in the manner prescribed by the Sec-
1
retary of Homeland Security, of the following events: 
2
(1) Such a worker fails to report to work within 
3
5 workdays of the employment start date on the pe-
4
tition or within 5 workdays of the date on which the 
5
worker is admitted into the United States pursuant 
6

7
(2) The labor or services for which such a work-
8

9
than the employment end date stated on the peti-
10

11
(3) The employment of such a worker is termi-
12

13
which he or she was hired. 
14
(4) Such a worker has not reported for work 
15
for a period of 5 consecutive workdays without the 
16

17
(b) EVIDENCE.—An employer shall retain evidence of 
18
a notification described in subsection (a) and make it 
19

20
Homeland Security for a 1-year period beginning on the 
21
date of the notification. 
22
(c) PENALTY.—The Secretary shall impose civil mon-
23

24
tion and not to exceed $1,000 per violation, as the Sec-
25
04:01 Mar 04, 2022
H6637
412 
•HR 6637 IH
retary determines to be appropriate, for each instance 
1

2

3

4

5
for the untimely notification, and the Secretary of Home-
6

7

8
(d) PROCESS.—If the Secretary has determined that 
9
an employer has violated the notification requirements in 
10
subsection (a), the employer shall be given written notice 
11
and 30 days to reply before being given written notice of 
12

13
(e) FAILURE TO PAY PENALTY.—If a penalty de-
14

15
sessment, no nonimmigrant or immigrant petition may be 
16

17

SEC. 204. PORTABLE H–2A VISA PILOT PROGRAM. 
3
(a) ESTABLISHMENT OF PILOT PROGRAM.— 
4
(1) IN GENERAL.—Not later than 18 months 
5
after the date of the enactment of this Act, the Sec-
6
retary of Homeland Security, in consultation with 
7
the Secretary of Labor and the Secretary of Agri-
8
culture, shall establish through regulation a 6-year 
9
pilot program to facilitate the free movement and 
10
employment of H–2A workers to perform agricul-
11
tural labor or services for agricultural employers 
12
registered with the Secretary of Agriculture. Not-
13
withstanding the requirements of section 218 of the 
14
Immigration and Nationality Act, such regulation 
15
shall establish the requirements for the pilot pro-
16
gram, consistent with subsection (b). For purposes 
17
of this section, such a worker shall be referred to as 
18
a portable H–2A worker, and status as such a work-
19
er shall be referred to as portable H–2A status. 
20
(2) ONLINE
PLATFORM.—The Secretary of 
21
Homeland Security, in consultation with the Sec-
22
retary of Labor and the Secretary of Agriculture, 
23
shall maintain an online electronic platform to con-
24
nect portable H–2A workers with registered agricul-
25
04:01 Mar 04, 2022
H6637
479 
•HR 6637 IH
tural employers seeking workers to perform agricul-
1
tural labor or services. Employers shall post on the 
2
platform available job opportunities, including a de-
3
scription of the nature and location of the work to 
4
be performed, the anticipated period or periods of 
5
need, and the terms and conditions of employment. 
6
Such platform shall allow portable H–2A workers to 
7
search for available job opportunities using relevant 
8
criteria, including the types of jobs needed to be 
9
filled and the dates and locations of need. 
10
(3) 
LIMITATION.—Notwithstanding 
the 
11

12

13

18

19
